<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="English">English</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=goose&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: English"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="sister-wikipedia sister-project noprint floatright" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 90%; background: #f9f9f9; width: 250px; padding: 4px; text-align: left;"><div style="float: left;"><figure class="mw-halign-none" typeof="mw:File"><span><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Wikipedia-logo-v2.svg/44px-Wikipedia-logo-v2.svg.png" decoding="async" width="44" height="40" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Wikipedia-logo-v2.svg/66px-Wikipedia-logo-v2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Wikipedia-logo-v2.svg/88px-Wikipedia-logo-v2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="103" data-file-height="94"></span><figcaption></figcaption></figure></div><div style="margin-left: 60px;">English <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia" title="Wikipedia">Wikipedia</a> has an article on:<div style="margin-left: 10px;"><b class="Latn" lang="en"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/goose_(disambiguation)" class="extiw" title="w:goose (disambiguation)">goose</a></b></div></div><span class="interProject"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/goose_(disambiguation)" class="extiw" title="w:goose (disambiguation)">Wikipedia </a></span></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=goose&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Etymology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="wikitable floatright PIE-word" style="text-align: center;"><tbody><tr><th>PIE word</th></tr><tr><td><span class="Latn" lang="ine-pro"><a href="/wiki/Reconstruction:Proto-Indo-European/%C7%B5%CA%B0h%E2%82%82%C3%A9ns" title="Reconstruction:Proto-Indo-European/ǵʰh₂éns">*ǵʰh₂éns</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_English" class="extiw" title="w:Middle English">Middle English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm"><a href="/wiki/goos#Middle_English" title="goos">goos</a></i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm"><a href="/wiki/gos#Middle_English" title="gos">gos</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_English" class="extiw" title="w:Old English">Old English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="ang"><a href="/wiki/gos#Old_English" title="gos">gōs</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-West_Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-West Germanic language">Proto-West Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="gmw-pro"><a href="/wiki/Reconstruction:Proto-West_Germanic/gans" title="Reconstruction:Proto-West Germanic/gans">*gans</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="gem-pro"><a href="/wiki/Reconstruction:Proto-Germanic/gans" title="Reconstruction:Proto-Germanic/gans">*gans</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="ine-pro"><a href="/wiki/Reconstruction:Proto-Indo-European/%C7%B5%CA%B0h%E2%82%82%C3%A9ns" title="Reconstruction:Proto-Indo-European/ǵʰh₂éns">*ǵʰh₂éns</a></i>.
</p>
<div class="NavFrame">
<div class="NavHead" style="text-align: left; cursor: pointer;"><span class="NavToggle"><a role="button" tabindex="0">show ▼</a></span>Cognates:</div>
<div class="NavContent derivedterms ul-column-count" data-column-count="2" style="text-align: left; display: none;">
Compare <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Frisian_language" class="extiw" title="w:West Frisian language">West Frisian</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fy"><a href="/wiki/goes#West_Frisian" title="goes">goes</a></i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Frisian_language" class="extiw" title="w:North Frisian language">North Frisian</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="frr"><a href="/w/index.php?title=g%C3%B6is&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="göis (page does not exist)">göis</a></i> (also Fering-Öömrang dialect <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Frisian_language" class="extiw" title="w:North Frisian language">North Frisian</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" <ul><li>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=tailor%27s_iron&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="tailor's iron (page does not exist)">tailor's iron</a> is so called from the likeness of the handle to the neck of a goose.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pronunciation">Pronunciation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=goose&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Pronunciation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Appendix:English_pronunciation" title="Appendix:English pronunciation">enPR</a>: <span class="AHD enPR">gōōs</span>, <a href="/wiki/Wiktionary:International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="Wiktionary:International Phonetic Alphabet">IPA</a><sup>(<a href="/wiki/Appendix:English_pronunciation" title="Appendix:English pronunciation">key</a>)</sup>: <span class="IPA">/ˈɡuːs/</span></li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=goose&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Noun"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Canada_goose_flight_cropped_and_NR.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Canada_goose_flight_cropped_and_NR.jpg/220px-Canada_goose_flight_cropped_and_NR.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="115" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Canada_goose_flight_cropped_and_NR.jpg/330px-Canada_goose_flight_cropped_and_NR.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Canada_goose_flight_cropped_and_NR.jpg/440px-Canada_goose_flight_cropped_and_NR.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1440" data-file-height="750"></a><figcaption>Canadian goose</figcaption></figure>
<p><span class="headword-line"><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en">goose</strong> (<i><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#countable" title="Appendix:Glossary">countable</a> and <a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#uncountable" title="Appendix:Glossary">uncountable</a></i>, <i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/geese#English" title="geese">geese</a></b>)</span>
</p>
<ol><li>Any of various grazing <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/waterfowl#English" title="waterfowl">waterfowl</a> of the family <span class="biota"><a href="/wiki/Anatidae#Translingual" title="Anatidae">Anatidae</a></span>, which have feathers and webbed feet and are capable of flying, swimming, and walking on land, and which are bigger than <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/duck#English" title="duck">ducks</a>.
<dl><dd><i>There is a flock of <b>geese</b> on the pond.</i></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="usage-label-sense"><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#strictly" title="Appendix:Glossary">strictly</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span></span> A <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/female#English" title="female">female</a> goose.
<span class="HQToggle" style="margin-left: 5px;"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations&nbsp;▼</a></span><ul style="display: none;"><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><span class="None" lang="und"><b>1902</b></span>, Lewis Wright, “Geese and Swans”, in <cite>The New Book of Poultry<span class="q-hellip-sp">&nbsp;</span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">[</span></span><span title="by Lewis Wright with Forty-Five Plates in Colour and Black and White by J. W. Ludlow and the Poultry Club Standards of Perfection for the Various Breeds">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">]</span></span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span></cite>, London, <span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">[</span></span><span title="Paris; New York, N.Y.; Melbourne, Vic.">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">]</span></span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span>: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cassell_(publisher)" class="extiw" title="w:Cassell (publisher)">Cassell and Company, Limited</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/cu31924003073248/page/560/mode/1up">page <span class="None" lang="und">560</span></a>, column 1:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation cited-passage" lang="en">Ganders and <b>geese</b> are at their best for stock from two to ten years old. They live to a great age—it is stated to thirty or more years—but after ten years they cannot be reckoned upon as reliable assets on a farm. Two years old is the best age to mate them, making up pens of a gander and two or three <b>geese</b> at the New Year. It is difficult sometimes to distinguish ganders from <b>geese</b>. A practical man is, however, rarely mistaken.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li>The flesh of the goose used as food.
<span class="HQToggle" style="margin-left: 5px;"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations&nbsp;▼</a></span><ul style="display: none;"><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><span class="None" lang="und"><b>1843</b></span>, Charles Dickens, “<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/A_Christmas_Carol_(Dickens,_1843)/Stave_3" class="extiw" title="s:A Christmas Carol (Dickens, 1843)/Stave 3">Stave 3: The Second of the Three Spirits</a>”, in <cite>A Christmas Carol</cite>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation cited-passage" lang="en">Mrs. Cratchit made the gravy (ready beforehand in a little saucepan) hissing hot; Master Peter mashed the potatoes with incredible vigour; Miss Belinda sweetened up the apple-sauce; Martha dusted the hot plates; Bob took Tiny Tim beside him in a tiny corner at the table; the two young Cratchits set chairs for everybody, not forgetting themselves, and mounting guard upon their posts, crammed spoons into their mouths, lest they should shriek for <b>goose</b> before their turn came to be helped.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="usage-label-sense"><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#slang" title="Appendix:Glossary">slang</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> plural <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/geese#English" title="geese">geese</a></i> or <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/gooses#English" title="gooses">gooses</a></i></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span></span> A silly person.
<span class="HQToggle" style="margin-left: 5px;"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations&nbsp;▼</a></span><ul style="display: none;"><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><span class="None" lang="und"><b>1906</b></span>, Langdon Mitchell, “The New York Idea”, in John Gassner, editor, <cite>Best Plays of the Early American Theatre, 1787-1911</cite>‎<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=xVSJZKaX3ScC">[1]</a></sup>, published <span class="None" lang="und">2000</span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0486410986" title="Special:BookSources/0486410986">→ISBN</a></small>, page <span class="None" lang="und">430</span>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation cited-passage" lang="en">I'm sorry for you, but you're such a <b>goose</b>.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><span class="None" lang="und"><b>1994</b></span>, Barbara Benedict, <cite>Love and Honor</cite>, New York, N.Y.: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jove_Books" class="extiw" title="w:Jove Books">Jove Books</a>, <small><a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-515-11312-3" title="Special:BookSources/0-515-11312-3">→ISBN</a></small>, page <span class="None" lang="und">65</span>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation cited-passage" lang="en">Have you stopped to think, you <b>gooses</b>, that Andy might not wish you to give it away?</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><span class="None" lang="und"><b>2014</b></span>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Julie_Berry_(author)" class="extiw" title="w:Julie Berry (author)">Julie Berry</a>, <cite>The Scandalous Sisterhood of Prickwillow Place</cite>, New York, N.Y.: Roaring Brook Press, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holtzbrinck_Publishing_Group" class="extiw" title="w:Holtzbrinck Publishing Group">Holtzbrinck Publishing Holdings Limited Partnership</a>, <small><a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-59643-957-3" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-59643-957-3">→ISBN</a></small>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation cited-passage" lang="en">You <b>gooses</b>. <i>I</i> didn’t accept his proposal. Mrs Plackett did. She did because she would. Don’t you see?</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><span class="None" lang="und"><b>2019</b></span>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Julia_London" class="extiw" title="w:Julia London">Julia London</a>, <cite>The Princess Plan</cite>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harlequin_Enterprises" class="extiw" title="w:Harlequin Enterprises">HQN Books</a>, <small><a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-474-09902-8" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-474-09902-8">→ISBN</a></small>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation cited-passage" lang="en">Surely I needn’t explain to you <b>gooses</b> that <i>none</i> of you, not even <i>you</i>, Caro, have the sort of dowry or connections or the <i>appeal</i> that such a match would require.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="usage-label-sense"><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#archaic" title="Appendix:Glossary">archaic</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span></span> A tailor's <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/iron#English" title="iron">iron</a>, heated in live coals or embers, used to press fabrics.
<span class="nyms-toggle" style="margin-left: 5px;"><a>synonym&nbsp;▲</a></span><span class="HQToggle" style="margin-left: 5px;"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations&nbsp;▼</a></span><dl><dd><span class="nyms synonym"><span class="defdate">Synonym:</span> <span class="Latn" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/goose_iron#English" title="goose iron">goose iron</a></span></span></dd></dl>
<ul style="display: none;"><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><i><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#c." title="Appendix:Glossary"><abbr title="circa">c.</abbr></a></i> <span class="None" lang="und"><b>1606</b></span> (date written), <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Shakespeare" class="extiw" title="w:William Shakespeare">William Shakespeare</a>, “<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Macbeth" class="extiw" title="w:Macbeth">The Tragedie of Macbeth</a>”, in <cite>Mr. William Shakespeares Comedies, Histories, &amp; Tragedies<span class="q-hellip-sp">&nbsp;</span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">[</span></span><span title="Published According to the True Originall Copies.">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">]</span></span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span></cite> (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Folio" class="extiw" title="w:First Folio">First Folio</a>), London: <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">[</span></span><span title="Printed by">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">]</span></span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Jaggard" class="extiw" title="w:William Jaggard">Isaac Iaggard</a>, and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_Blount" class="extiw" title="w:Edward Blount">Ed<span style="font-style: normal;">[</span>ward<span style="font-style: normal;">]</span> Blount</a>, published <span class="None" lang="und">1623</span>, <small><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.worldcat.org/title/606515358">→OCLC</a></small>, <span style="font-style: normal;">[</span>Act II, scene iii<span style="font-style: normal;">]</span>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation cited-passage" lang="en">Come in, tailor. Here you may roast your <b>goose</b>.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="usage-label-sense"><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_African_English" class="extiw" title="w:South African English">South Africa</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#slang" title="Appendix:Glossary">slang</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#dated" title="Appendix:Glossary">dated</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span></span> A <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/young#English" title="young">young</a> <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/woman#English" title="woman">woman</a> or <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/girlfriend#English" title="girlfriend">girlfriend</a>.</li>
<li><span class="usage-label-sense"><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#uncountable" title="Appendix:Glossary">uncountable</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#historical" title="Appendix:Glossary">historical</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span></span> An old English <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/board_game#English" title="board game">board game</a> in which players moved counters along a board, earning a double move when they reached the picture of a goose.</li></ol>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hypernyms">Hypernyms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=goose&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Hypernyms"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=goose&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Verb"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><span class="headword-line"><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en">goose</strong> (<i>third-person singular simple present</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en s-verb-form-form-of" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/gooses#English" title="gooses">gooses</a></b>, <i>present participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en ing-form-form-of" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/goosing#English" title="goosing">goosing</a></b>, <i>simple past and past participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en ed-form-form-of" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/goosed#English" title="goosed">goosed</a></b>)</span>
</p>
<ol><li><span class="usage-label-sense"><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#transitive" title="Appendix:Glossary">transitive</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#slang" title="Appendix:Glossary">slang</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span></span> To sharply poke or pinch the buttocks, or prod between the buttocks, of (a person).
<span class="HQToggle" style="margin-left: 5px;"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations&nbsp;▼</a></span><ul style="display: none;"><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><span class="None" lang="und"><b>1933</b></span>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nathanael_West" class="extiw" title="w:Nathanael West">Nathanael West</a>, <cite>Miss Lonelyhearts</cite>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation cited-passage" lang="en">She greeted Miss Lonelyhearts, then took hold of her husband and shook the breath out of him. When he was quiet, she dragged him into their apartment. Miss Lonelyhearts followed and as he passed her in the dark foyer, she <b>goosed</b> him and laughed.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><span class="None" lang="und"><b>1963</b></span>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J_P_Donleavy" class="extiw" title="w:J P Donleavy">J P Donleavy</a>, <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/A_Singular_Man" class="extiw" title="w:A Singular Man">A Singular Man</a></cite>, published <span class="None" lang="und">1963 (USA)</span>, page <span class="None" lang="und">36</span>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation cited-passage" lang="en">The witness stand. Goldminers giving evidence, sure he's violent didn't I see him with my own peepers chasing those poor kids up on the roof and he <b>goosed</b> my wife last Christmas. Violently. Just a forceful nudge of the knee.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1991</b> August 24, Artemis OakGrove, “I Deserve A Medal”, in <cite>Gay Community News</cite>, volume <span class="None" lang="und">19</span>, number 6, page 5:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation cited-passage" lang="en">Here are the three strange men have exposed themselves to me, the two obscene phone callers, the time I was <b>goosed</b> by an employer.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="usage-label-sense"><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#transitive" title="Appendix:Glossary">transitive</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#slang" title="Appendix:Glossary">slang</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span></span> To <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/stimulate#English" title="stimulate">stimulate</a>; to <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/spur#English" title="spur">spur</a>.
<span class="HQToggle" style="margin-left: 5px;"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations&nbsp;▼</a></span><ul style="display: none;"><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2021</b> December 7, Jesse Hassenger, “<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leonardo_DiCaprio" class="extiw" title="w:Leonardo DiCaprio">Leonardo DiCaprio</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jennifer_Lawrence" class="extiw" title="w:Jennifer Lawrence">Jennifer Lawrence</a> cope with disaster in the despairing satire <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Don%27t_Look_Up_(2021_film)" class="extiw" title="w:Don't Look Up (2021 film)">Don’t Look Up</a></i>”, in <cite>AV Club</cite>‎<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.avclub.com/leonardo-dicaprio-and-jennifer-lawrence-cope-with-disas-1848171832">[2]</a></sup>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation cited-passage" lang="en">Almost everyone in McKay’s impossibly starry cast feels like they’re jumping into the <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" class="extiw" title="w:Saturday Night Live">SNL</a></i> host role, game for some light comedic lifting while waiting for the pros to show up and <b>goose</b> the laughs.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2023</b> July 10, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Poniewozik" class="extiw" title="w:James Poniewozik">James Poniewozik</a>, “The Twitter Watch Party Is Over”, in <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_New_York_Times" class="extiw" title="w:The New York Times">The New York Times</a></cite>‎<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2023/07/10/arts/television/tv-twitter-end-of-an-era.html">[3]</a></sup>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation cited-passage" lang="en">The ensuing snarknado also seemed to <b>goose</b> the TV ratings. Hundreds of thousands of viewers switched on the movie after it began, suggesting that they’d gotten wind through Twitter of the bananas spectacle that was unfolding.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="usage-label-sense"><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#transitive" title="Appendix:Glossary">transitive</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#slang" title="Appendix:Glossary">slang</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span></span> To gently accelerate (an automobile or machine), or give repeated small taps on the accelerator.</li>
<li><span class="usage-label-sense"><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#slang" title="Appendix:Glossary">slang</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_English" class="extiw" title="w:British English">UK</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span></span> Of private-hire <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/taxi#English" title="taxi">taxi</a> drivers, to pick up a passenger who has not booked a cab, in violation of UK licensing conditions.</li>
<li><span class="usage-label-sense"><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#transitive" title="Appendix:Glossary">transitive</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#slang" title="Appendix:Glossary">slang</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span></span> To <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/hiss#English" title="hiss">hiss</a> (a performer) off the stage.</li></ol>
